RE: Prior Year Deficiency Report—FY2026, Quarter 3
Dear Chair Michlewitz and Chair Rodrigues:
In accordance with Item 1599-2040 of Section 2B of Chapter 9 of the Acts of 2025, the Office of
the Comptroller hereby submits the attached Paid Prior Year Deficiency Report (the Report) on
prior year deficiencies to the Senate and House Committees on Ways and Means.
The Report contains information regarding payment of prior year deficiencies through chargebacks
to Fiscal Year 2026 funds.
Through the third quarter of Fiscal Year 2026, as detailed in the attached report, a total of
$14,188,117.65 was spent in prior year deficiencies for 41 departments. Of that amount,
$3,970,347.40 was incurred in accounts that had sufficient funds (the department reverted funds
to the General Fund at the end of Fiscal Year 2025) and $10,217,770.25 was from accounts that
had insufficient funds (the department did not revert funds to the General Fund at the end of Fiscal
Year 2025). Whether there were sufficient or insufficient funds, the funding for prior year
deficiencies is recouped from each department’s current year appropriation.
- Page 1 of 2 -

*Insufficient Funds
Reason # of # of
Reason Short Description
Code Occurrences Depts
Billing dispute can take a lengthy time to settle. During the ongoing negotiation to resolve a dispute, the FY in which the
BD Billing Dispute 0 0
payment should have been made would be closed.
There are instances when vendor invoices are submitted after the close of the FY. There are several reasons, such as, the
LI vendor invoice was never sent, sent late or lost in the mail or the department did not recognize or reconcile outstanding Late Invoice 2,582 38
invoices before the close of the FY.
Unexpected bills are costs incurred by vendors on behalf of departments often to prevent business disruption. An example
would be malfunction/break of heating/cooling systems. Incidents such as this would require immediate
UB Unexpected Billing 0 0
repair/replacement without proper review of funding source. When such incidents occur the department usually, either
files a supplemental budget or will settle with a departmental PYD.
Misplaced/lost Invoices most often occurs with agencies that have regional offices. Vendors may ship their invoices to
MI regional offices for review and authorization. Regional offices then send the invoices to central office for payment. In Misplaced/lost Invoice 18 2
between the regional offices and the central office, bills could be lost or misplaced.
This type of error occurs when a department copies forward a PRC and the data entry person forgets to change the vendor
AE code from the PRC and submits the PRC to final. In this instance the wrong vendor will be paid. Unless the department Accounting Error 4 2
finds out before the end of the FY and pay the correct vendor, it would be required to process PYD.
There are specific instances where departments are required to provide services without the availability of sufficient funds.
Insufficient Funds
IF The vendor completes the task and submits an invoice. The department pursues legislative funding solution. For prior year 450 4
Encumbered
invoices outstanding the PYD process may be used as well.
